**Chapter LXV.**
**Of the Treatment of Intestinal Hernia.**
Hernia occurs due to a rupture in the abdominal wall caused by straining during bowel movements, allowing intestines to protrude.
And this rupture occurs either in the abdominal wall itself or due to an exit from it. This happens for many reasons such as: percussion, sneezing, coughing, heavy lifting, or similar causes.
And the sign of this is that if it occurs due to an extension of the abdominal wall, it happens gradually over time and not suddenly. It appears as a swelling between the pubic area and the groin because the abdominal wall compresses the intestines.
And the sign of it is that if it occurs due to a rupture of the abdominal wall, initially there is sudden severe pain. It appears as a different visible swelling near the groin area, which is due to protrusion of the intestines through the rent in the abdominal wall.
Sometimes the intestinal tissue becomes trapped outside the abdominal cavity without being able to be pushed back inside. This type of hernia is called an incarcerated or strangulated hernia.
Sometimes there is windiness (flatulence), sometimes the intestine slips out of the rent and gets trapped inside it. This can cause great danger to one's health. Sometimes it causes severe pain, especially when pressed upon.
And in the treatment of these types of diseases with iron, caution is necessary to avoid causing a hemorrhage at that location.
The procedure for this operation is as follows: tell the patient to push their abdomen inward with both hands from inside the navel if it returns there. Then quickly place your hands on their thighs and lift them up. This will help reduce the hernia by pushing the intestines back into the abdominal cavity.
Then press the cord that connects the scrotum to the abdominal wall at its base, and incise it along its length. Then use two forceps on either side of the incision to widen the opening as much as necessary to expose the hernia.
And if the incision is made wide enough according to your ability, the protruding loop of intestine may be able to slip back into place on its own.
Then carefully remove the fluid-filled sac that is surrounding the loop of intestine (hernial sac) by pushing it back through the opening in the abdominal wall until only the white fibrous tissue of each side remains exposed.
Then insert your finger into the opening around the testicle, between the white fibrous tissue (which is left attached to the loop of intestine) and the hernial sac. Then carefully separate any adhesions that may be present behind the hernia with your finger.
Then grasp the cord with your left hand at its base on the outside, and stretch the white fibrous tissue upwards with your right hand. Then lift the loop of intestine along with the hernial sac back into the abdomen through the incision. Tell your assistant to hold the loop of intestine in place from above while you use warm saline solution to dissolve any remaining adhesions behind it.
Carefully check with your fingers that there is no bowel tissue still wrapped around the white fibrous cord (hernial sac) and that it has been completely reduced into the abdomen. But if you find any remaining cause (tissue), then carefully push it back into the abdominal cavity with your fingers.
Then incise along the spermatic cord on its lateral side, as previously described, to allow blood and lymph fluid to drain freely.
Then apply sterile gauze soaked in oil to the wound and place it over the incision. Then apply a ligature as previously described (and occasionally cauterize the white fibrous tissue with a hot iron near the blood vessel tie-off, especially if there is active bleeding), and leave the ligature in place until it falls off on its own.
But if the wound does not close spontaneously, then apply hot water compresses to promote healing and reduce inflammation as previously described.
Then dress the wound using appropriate wound care techniques until it is healed.
Chapter LXVI
On Ventral Hernia
In this type of hernia, there is nothing that can be burned or cauterized during the operation.
The early authors said that it should be treated in the same way as a hernia with fluid (hydrocele), by ligating and tying off the blood vessels around the hernia and then cauterizing the wound with a hot iron to prevent infection.
And dress the wound according to what has been said until it is healed.
Chapter LXVII
On Dislocation of the Jaw
Sometimes there occurs rupture in the joints as we have said, and swellings appear at that location.
And if the intestines do not cause any problem to the horse, then that is good, and it returns to its usual state at all times.
But if the time is prolonged thus, there occurs an adjustable fissure in the hip joint through which the intestine enters into the hip joint; and this happens because of the extension of the hip joint which is located in the joints as we have said, whose cause is that the hip joint has been stretched out and the place becomes softened, with the resulting apostema (an abscess) and swelling.
And its cure is through cauterization as it has been preceded by its narration.
And sometimes it is cured with iron according to this manner: and it is that the sick person lays upon his back between two pillows, and then the place of rupture of the swellings is dried up by section through its width according to their quantity.
And then strengthen the white hip joint which is below the backbone so that it may be discovered (i.e., brought back into alignment).
And then take the ray and place it upon the prominent part of the hip joint, and press it against the front of the belly.
And then heat the two prominent places upon the end of the ray of the hip joint, and join them together with a suture.
And then extract the end of the ray, and do not squeeze the hip joint at all, nor extend the wound, nor cause any other harm as you know well in the cure of intestinal hernia.
And then cure it with the cure of ulcers, and when you have cut through the tissues, cleanse them and restore the ulcer so that it may be consolidated; because the hip joint is contracted and the prominence of rupture is not joined together.
And cauterization is better in this place, for it is closer to health.
"Chapter 68."
"The softening of the chain of the testicles."
"Many times the chain of the testicles in some men is softened because the flesh that is between them is softened. This is noticed."
"Therefore it is necessary that whoever examines the treatment of this [condition] makes the patient lie on their back, and cuts all the softened chain along its length above the natural chain; then he should approximate both lips with stitches."
"And if you wish, at the beginning, remove the excess of the softened chain with three or four cuts and sew it firmly."
"And then cut between the sutures; and then treat with treatment for other diseases until healed, and the threads fall out."
"Chapter 69."
"The Castration."
"Know that castration is condemned in our law, but because it has been requested of me that I remember this in this book, and it is not necessary to remember it except for two ways: the first is so that it may be known by those who study medicine when they are asked about this, that they may know its treatment; and the second way is that we often have a need for castration of other beasts for our uses for those animals, such as mules, goats, pigs, and similar beasts."
"And therefore I say that castration is done in two ways: either by crushing or by cutting through a section."
When an injury is caused by a blow, the method of treatment is to seize the beast in heated water until its genitals are softened and made limp, and then suspend it. And furthermore take those with your hand so that they are resolved and do not appear outside the touching point.
Moreover, in castration performed through incision and sectioning, you should hold the beast and press the cord of its testicles with your left hand.
And moreover tie the suspensory ligament, and make an incision over each one with a section so that two halves proceed from it.
And moreover cut those parts that will have extruded outwards. Do not leave anything on the scrotum except for the thin skin which is above the testicles.
And this method of castration is better than the one performed by crushing because crushing leaves no trace of the testicles and makes the beast desire copulation.
And furthermore treat the wound until it is healed.
"Chapter Seventy."
"On the Treatment of Hermaphroditism."
"In men, hermaphroditism occurs in two ways: the first is when it appears in that space between the testicles where it resembles a vulva with menstrual blood."
"And sometimes urine flows from that area between the testicles."
"In women, it is one species: and that is when the vulva on the pubis appears like two testicles of a man, a little bit smaller at their opening, like the penis of a man and two testicles."
"And its treatment is of three kinds: two for men and one for women." "And you should insert those joined flesh between the opening of that (vulva) and cure it with the cure for other sores."
"And in the second kind of men where urine flows from between the testicles, there is neither cure nor operation for it."

"Chapter LXXIV."
"Of the Perforation of an Abscess Accidentally in the Belly."
Many kinds of ulcers occur on the thigh, such as hard and fleshy tumors, ulcers, inflamed sores, scabs, serpiginous fistulas, blood-filled cavities, and others. I have already spoken about these illnesses, their types, symptoms, and treatments in the chapter on ulcers.
And now I will explain in this treatise how to cauterize the ulcer that appears on the thigh when it comes from ulcers that do not heal, and if you wish to know how the operation is performed with iron.
Therefore, you should consider whether the pain of the ulcer at its beginning is acute with percussion and swelling and fever, if it becomes reddened and tender to the touch. Then, do not cut into it with a cautery until it begins to mature, and treat it with water that helps with maturation until the sharpness of the symptoms ceases.
"Now you must place the woman on an elevated surface that has two pillows; she should recline on her back and adjust her feet close to the opening of her womb, with her thighs spread wide. Then position her arms beside her breasts, binding each one appropriately."

Chapter LXXV.
"To teach midwives how to treat women whose births are difficult and do not proceed according to nature."
"It is necessary that the midwife recognizes at the beginning the figure of a natural birth by its signs, and this happens when she sees the woman pressing her thighs together and desiring to smell the air, and afterwards she feels relieved by what comes out over her, and hastens the birth of the child; then you know that this birth is according to nature. And this is the emergence of the head first, followed by the shoulders hanging from it or suspended from the umbilical cord."
"Therefore, when you see those signs, it is necessary that the woman's belly is pressed so that the child comes out gently as it emerges over its head; then the shoulders follow, and they are cleaned of those excesses with good cleansing."
"But if the birth is not according to nature and is not desirable, then it occurs when the child emerges feet first, with its body emerging before its head and feet; or one of its hands emerges first, or its foot, or its head emerges together with its hand or belly. And thus it turns upside down on its neck, resembling those figures that are not desirable."
"Therefore, it is necessary for the midwife to be wise and subtle in all of these causes and to guard against error and deception."
"And here we are showing you all the figures of those that are not according to nature, and what is their cause, so that it may be understood by this and established on this."
"When the feet emerge first due to an error of nature, and it is violent over the woman and difficult for her to give birth, and she sees that her strength has weakened, then they should seize it by its feet or what the women hold onto, and evaporate its head with fenugreek cooked in oil and humid earth."
"And also the midwife should insert herself between its legs and tear open the second with her finger or cut it open with her fingernail until what is inside it of humidity flows out." "And press the woman's belly until the child comes out."
"But if it does not come out, then the woman should be crystallized with dough of barley and dough of fenugreek with sesame."
"And then command her to be pressed, and also she should sneeze with conditions; and put your mouth over hers and your nose over hers for one hour, because the child will soon forget."
"And if both arms of the child are forgotten at the beginning, then you should reduce them gently little by little." "But if it does not obey the manipulation, then place the woman on a pillow and lift her feet up, and also strike the pillow against the ground so that the woman is held that she does not fall due to the blow."
"And if the arms are not properly returned and the child dies, then incise those veins and extract the flesh of the child or tie its body to your hand with cloth and extract it equally, because that will soon forget."
"When the child emerges feet first, then you should push those up and also turn the child gently around, and grasp its heel with your finger, and take one of its feet and stretch it out little by little."
"But when it is inside the hips, then you should command it to press itself out and make it sneeze with conditions, because it will soon forget if God wishes."
"And if it is not forgotten with what we have recommended, then return the child gently little by little until you place it according to natural figure, because that will soon forget at that moment with gentle birth."
"And if it is prohibited with all that we have recommended, then take dough of mallow and dissolved gum, and grind everything well in the mortar, and also line the woman's head, especially the lower part of her belly." "And also make her drink hot water decoction until she achieves contractions."
"When the passages of the child are softened, then make it steam with myrtle and keep it warm." "And when it has had steam for one hour, then make her lie down on a pillow and make her sneeze and draw out her mouth, take that out from there, and press the lower part of the birth passage gently because the child will soon forget."

Chapter LXXVI
Of the extraction of the dead fetus
When you care for the dead fetus as we have said in the division of midwifery and it has not yet been expelled, and you are forced to use an operation with your hand, then you must consider if the woman is of good health and does not have any of the accidents by which loss may be feared over her.
Then the woman must be placed on her left side on the bed, and her head should be inclined downwards and her hips raised.
And the attendant must hold her from both parts or else she must lie on the bed so that her body does not extend during the extraction of the fetus.
And then you must moisten the mouth of the womb with olive oil and with mucilage of marsh mallow, fenugreek, and linseed.
And then the midwife should anoint her hand with those oils and mucilages, and then she should insert her hand gently into the womb, and then she should search with her hand for where the hook is located in the fetus.
And the convenient place for this is: then consider if the fetus is ready to be expelled on its head, and then you should place the hook in the fetus' ears or neck or mouth or palate or beard or furcula or near the ribs or below the hypochondria.
But if the expulsion is on its feet, then in the perineum or middle of the buttocks.
And it is necessary to hold the hook with the right hand, and place its curve in that location which is between the fingers of the left hand, and insert the hand gently until you reach the desired cause of the child's body.
And then hold and place another hook or the third one if necessary, in order to have equal traction and not just lengthwise extension according to its correctness.
And may it be useful for all deliveries, so that the expulsion of the fetus is alleviated just as it happens in tooth extraction during its eradication.
And it is necessary that during this the extension should be softened; and if any part of the fetus is retained, then the midwife must anoint some of her fingers with oil and insert them gently and turn them around in what is retained.
Therefore if the expulsion of the fetus has not happened yet, then the hooks should be changed to another place where they may push more effectively; and do this until the entire fetus has been expelled.
But if the hand has come out before the other, and it is not possible to reduce it by its contraction, then cloth should be wrapped around it; and then extract it until all of it has been expelled, and cut it off either at the junction of the hand or in the elbow.
And do the same with the other hand and both feet.
But if the head of the fetus is large, or it occurs contraction in its expulsion, or there is water in the head of the child, then you must insert between the spinous processes of the pubic bones and split open the head and extract the water, or remove it with an instrument called "alundat", the form of which will come with the forms of other instruments in the chapter that follows this one.
And do the same if the fetus has a large head by nature: and then it is necessary to cut off that with an instrument called "gematu", or take it out with the alundat as we have said, and then extract the bones with forceps.
And if the head has been expelled but is contracted by the pubic arch, then it should be split open until the fluid in the fontanelle has flowed out.
But if it is not complicated and does not obey expulsion, then cut open the head immediately as much as you can manage on your own.
And if there is an aposteme or hydrops in the lower abdomen, then you must perforate it until the fluid in it runs out.
But if the fetus is lying on its back, then its attraction will be lighter and its direction to the mouth of the mother will be easier.
"If the belly and chest are tightly bound, then you must remove that cloth which you have wrapped around your hand, and cut into the belly and chest so that whatever is inside may flow out."
"If the other limbs are stretched out and the head is turned, then insert your left hand; but if the mouth of the mother is closed, then insert your hand into her throat, encircle the head with it, pull that towards those things [the limbs], and immediately put one or two fingers inside [the mouth] and push them in there."

"I have seen a woman whose fetus died in her womb, and again she became pregnant shortly thereafter, and the second fetus also died." "It happened that about a long time after an ulcer formed in her uterus; it became inflamed internally where it was opened, and began to emit a bad smell."
"And I was called for its treatment, and I treated it for a long time, but the illness did not resolve."
"Therefore I suspected that it might be caused by some sort of strong attraction, and I extracted one bone from it, and about a few days later, another bone was extracted; and I was very amazed because there are no bones in the uterus."
"And then I thought that they were the bones of the dead fetus."
"So I treated the illness, and extracted many bones from it, and the woman remained in good condition, living in that way for a long time without any bad odor coming from it."
"And I did not regard this as strange, because in this there is knowledge and assistance for the physician who performs cures with his own hand."

Of treating the imperforate anus of a child
Many children are born with imperforate anuses that are subtle and obstructed. Therefore it falls to the midwife to pierce this opening with her finger, and if not, then to pierce it with a sharp spike, taking care not to touch the intestine.
And she should place thereupon some wool soaked in wine and oil, and keep wiping until clean.
But if you fear it is obstructed, then place a catheter there for several days to drain, and remove it when the child wants to eat.
And if an obstruction of the anus occurs due to a collection of pus or an abscess, then it is necessary to incise that collection and similarly treat it with the remedies mentioned above for the lead.
Of treating fistulas that develop there.
Fistulas that develop near the passage of the anus, which are swollen and thickened, often occur close to the buttocks externally or in the space between the buttocks.
And it is a fistula or warts.
Moreover, when that swelling is chronic and comes from moist heat, it produces a white or clear yellowish fluid, and sometimes these fistulas have penetrating openings.
And these openings are recognized by what exits from them through the exit and via windiness; sometimes the disease manifests through discharge, and it is often discharged through worms.
Sometimes these fistulas have penetrating openings that extend into the bladder and into the urethra; some of these openings extend into the junction of the scrotum and into the glands of the penis.
And to recognize a penetrating or non-penetrating fistulous opening entering the anus, you should insert your little finger into the anus and carefully probe the fistula with a fine thread of silk or iron when there is no obstruction.
But if there is an obstruction, then insert a fine thread of lead or horsehair until you feel the thread or hair against your little finger.
And if you do not feel anything with it and find no cause for discharge or worms or windiness, as we have said before, then you should know that it is non-penetrating, and thus begin the treatment.
And when a fistula is penetrating into the bladder or into the urethra, then its significance is that urine will be discharged from it and there will be impediment to it until it becomes consolidated according to what is taught in medicine.
But if it is penetrating into the scrotum or into the bone and there is pain around it, then its sign is that the probe may penetrate here if there is no obstruction in the bone, and there will be pain around the opening; and that there is always purulent matter; and that medicine has no effect on it, nor does it become consolidated with ointments.
And in all penetrating fistulas there is no complete cure, and the treatment of these is merely the struggle and deception of foolish physicians, about which we are firmly convinced.
But in those that are not penetrating and do not open, healing with iron is expected according to what I will advise you, and that which I have already said.
And it is that the disease appears between your thighs, mainly on the right side and raises the scrotum within itself, with the testes inclining toward its abdomen, and carefully insert a probe of lead or silk if there is an obstruction in the fistula, until you know where the probe comes out.
And if that disease is felt around the anus, then it is necessary for you to insert your little finger into the anus in that direction.
And if you feel with your little finger that the probe is already openly penetrating inside, other than what you feel between your little finger and that siphac or flesh, then certainly know that that one is penetrating; and therefore do not struggle with it, for there is no healing of it, as we have said before.
But nevertheless some people say that it can be healed in certain men.
And the treatment by which it is hoped that some good may be achieved in it is this: cauterize with a subtle fire according to the width of the fistula, as has been described above, and insert that burning into the fistula until it reaches around the anus; and then repeat this two or three times until you know that all those adherent fistulous tissues have been burnt like the feathers of a bird.
And then dress it with hot fomentations wrapped in wool until all those adherent tissues have softened; and then treat it with medicines that generate and consolidate flesh, and if it heals, good. But if not, then know that it will never be healed by any other treatment.
And if the probe enters and does not penetrate inside your little finger which is in the anus and between that and the probe which is covered with flesh or siphac, sometimes the fistula goes along the surface of the bone, then cut the bone from the beginning of the fistula; and you will see it dry with the probe, and let it be in the fistula until the section reaches to where the end of the probe comes out; and through the probe it is freed and healed.
And then clean those fistulous tissues which are like the feathers of a bird's quill, and do not leave any of them behind.
But if there is bleeding that comes between you and your operation when you cut those tissues, then the milder instrument to cauterize with fire or with an acute medicine is better, for cautery with fire has good two habits: it is adhesion of those adherent tissues, and excision of blood and drying of moisture.
And then dress it with hot fomentations wrapped in wool or with thin cloth until that place becomes warm; and then afterwards treat the wound with hard flesh-generating and consolidating medicines.
And these are the medicines in which there is astringency and excision; when they are applied, it will be restored and already healed, with no fear of recurrence.
But if the fistula has already reached into the anus and extends along the surface of the body, then insert your little finger into the anus and explore with it.
And therefore if you feel the probe and there is something like siphac or flesh between you and it, and it is close to penetration, then there is no operation for it except according to the way of faith and hope.
And this is to be administered in it in one of three ways: either cauterize it as has been said; or cut it open until you achieve the concavity of it so that you can possibly insert your finger and apply the proposed treatment; and do not proceed with cutting too much, for fear of wounding the contents of the anus and causing pain and harm without cause. And then dress it with what has been said, for flesh is easily healed there. Or else elongate that velament and clean out that pus which dries it inside close to the anus as has been said, either with a probe or with another instrument of sharp point; and then clean those fistulous tissues which are in the section by scraping them away with a curette. And then strive to heal all the wound with stitching; and if the opened orifice does not consolidate above, and the fistula remains open at its beginning near the anus, it will cause pain. And sometimes the fistula is finished in this way: when you insert the probe into the fistula and it comes out on the side of the anus around the surface of the body with the bone and at the margin of the anus, then take a probe with a perforated tip, which is like a needle for preparing hearts, shaped thus:
"I will now introduce this needle into that opening of yours, turning them; and immediately I will try to insert another needle into the fistula until it reaches its cavity."
"But if you penetrate the margin of the anus properly, then you should remove that thread as such that you can insert your little finger into the anus; and after removing the end of the thread, join both ends together, strain each one separately, and leave it like this for a day or two, and whenever you notice that the thread has cut into the flesh, then carefully remove that part where those cuts are located which are between the two ends of the thread."
"And immediately heal the wound until it is consolidated and healed."
"But if the opening of the fistula is not penetrated, then you should make it penetrate in whatever manner you are prepared for, but do not probe too deeply into the perineum lest you injure the skin. And immediately apply that (ointment) until it is healed."
"The shape of the spatula with spines on which the fistula is opened has one end very sharp and the other end not sharp, so that you do not injure what is not necessary."
"Regarding the suture of hemorrhoids in which blood flows from the opening of those (hemorrhoids),"
"Hemorrhoids occur in two manners: either they are between the buttocks appearing like coal, or they seem to be filled with grease of rose hips." "And those are small and large, from which blood constantly flows and is one, and are numerous, and are outside the anus, and at its ends."
"But those that are outside the anus occur according to the months of little humidity, from which yellow water or a bit of blood runs continuously with the body's sweat, and they vary in color."
"And the treatment for that which is inside the anus is that you command the patient to sit up and press inward until the anus opens and the hemorrhoids appear before you." "Then you take and suspend with forceps or whatever you may have those [hemorrhoids] with your nail, and promptly cut them at their roots."
"But if the forceps do not hold those [hemorrhoids] due to their humidity and softness, then you take them with rough cloth or with cotton or with a wool pad, and extract those with your fingers, and promptly cut them at their roots and sprinkle some powdered resin thereupon immediately after cutting so that it may serve as cautery for those; or cauterize them according to what is stated in the chapter on cauterizing." "And afterwards dress those with the other dressing until they are healed."
"And if the anus does not obey evacuation, then you catheterize the patient with a catheter in which there is a small bite and let it be washed with that water which is in the anus so that it may facilitate easy evacuation when the patient presses."
"But if the hemorrhoids are outside the anus, then their cause is light, and it suffices that you take them with your nail or that you take them with forceps and cut them, and afterwards dress them with water as has been said until they are healed."
"And he who cuts them should administer suture to them in this manner: take a thread wrapped and insert it into the needle and then extract the hemorrhoids at their roots above, and make the thread penetrate with the needle into the root of the other part, and wrap the two ends of the thread around that part more distant from the needle, and stretch the hemorrhoid tightly with strong tension, and then tie the thread and remove the needle."
"And do this to all of them, leaving one alone without tying it so that the superfluous blood may flow out from it."
"And then apply over the anus a dressing made of lint soaked in rose oil or wax, and apply that over the anus and command the patient to repose." "And then leave it like that for three days; and when it is healed, dress it with ointment or with another dressing until it is completely healed."
And if those veins are old and not useful in that medicine, then you should open those with the point of a spatula or your nail so they are moistened and remove the thick pus above them which hinders their solidification. And immediately clean those that have been solidified.
Then you must remove it with a very strong razor so that at first there is no blood and they are not scraped. And immediately heal those that have been healed.
Know that the soul is the key, and not blood according to the color of the body resembling a small nail head. It is found throughout the body but more so in the joints of the legs and arms. Thereby pain occurs through them.
Therefore, it is necessary that what is in the circuit of the key be incised and held with forceps or tweezers, and eradicated from its root. And immediately heal it.
And if you wish, cauterize the second one that is mentioned in its chapter.
But warts are small, rough, flesh-colored elevations on the surface of the body, often rounded and sometimes pustular. Many are seen in children.
And the treatment for it is that you stretch out and incise it with a knife or scrape it off with a file or pumice stone until it bleeds freely. And if you wish, cauterize it with fire or with an acute medicine, as we have said before.
But a pimple is a small, fatty or pustular elevation on the surface of the body that often appears on the forehead and elsewhere. When it is pressed, it becomes inflamed like the sting of an ant, and it appears around the body.
And the treatment for it is that you take a quill from an ostrich or vulture feather and make it strong. Place it over the pimple so that its circle surrounds it. Then rotate your hand with the quill to incise what is in the circuit of the pimple, pressing it against the skin of the forehead. And eradicate the pimple from its root.
And if you wish, do this with a needle made of brass or iron in this way:
Let the point of the needle be drawn to a fine, blunt tip, not perforated, wrapped in such a way that when you grasp it with your fingers, its edge is smoothed and its rotation facilitated.
And if you wish to cauterize the pimple, do so according to what has been mentioned in the chapter on cautery concerning atheyl.
Of the instruments used for administering cautery
Sometimes cautery is performed with silver or lead that has been melted and hammered. And sometimes it is performed using instruments that are small or large according to those used for the purpose. For example, the one used in treating young children should be small; and for those whose bottoms are furrowed or wrinkled, their cauteries should also be small.
The method of performing a large cautery with little injury:
The opening of the cannula's head should be wide in this manner, and it should be at the distinction where the bag is tied in this way.
And the lower end of the tube that is inserted into the anus should be blunt (i.e., not open), tapering to a subtlety; and on one side there are two holes, and on the other side one hole, with the width of the hole according to the thickness of the rays.
And let the bag in which the medicines are placed be made from bladder or sheep's skin, and its width be one palm.
And let it be perforated with many holes so that it rotates evenly; and the distance between the holes should be roughly the thickness of a finger.
And then insert through those holes a strong thread of raw silk that is made from ten threads, or wind it around them; and adjust it with the bag. And when you place the bag on him, tighten it at the head of the clyster syringe between two distinctions with strong constriction, and clysterize with it through each hole: But the quality of clysterizing with it is that you should heat the bag of medicine according to the quantity of the patient's tolerance; and be careful not to make it too hot nor too cold.
And then the patient should lie on their back with their buttocks raised and place a cloth or towel underneath them to prevent staining of the bedding. Then anoint the tip of the clyster syringe with oil, albumen of egg white, or mucilage of fenugreek or similar substances. Then insert it into the anus gently, and then the attendant should take the bag and squeeze it two or three times forcefully until all the contents of the clyster syringe have been emptied into the bowel. Then remove the clyster syringe and the patient should raise their buttocks against the wall.
And if the medicine causes him to perspire excessively, let him hold as much of it in as he can. And if he sleeps with it for the whole night, it will be more effective in its benefit.
But if you clysterize him for loose bowels and diarrhea in which the excretion of the belly is copious, then repeat the clyster until he is healed.
And if there are hemorrhoids or tender fistulas in the anus, then let the clyster be very thin and gentle, of those clysters with which children are clysterized.
Regarding the treatment of plagues.
I have already said in the division on the treatment of plagues what was necessary for the book, and I say now the treatment of those with more severity using medicines according to their condition.
Therefore I say that plagues are diversified according to what part of the body they occur in and according to the location on which the plague manifests itself.
And the causes for which often plagues occur are such as: cutting with a spearhead, or incision with an razor blade or knife, or piercing with a lance, or beating with a club or stick, or being hit by an arrow, and similar accidents.
But the plagues which are in certain parts of the body are such as: plague that occurs on the head, or the neck, or the foot, or the belly, or the thigh, and similar ones on the limbs.
And I am now describing the treatment of certain plagues so that you may pause this reasoning and rule about the other plagues.
And I will begin with simple head plagues, for the reminder of the composite ones will come at the beginning of the third chapter.
Therefore I say that when a simple head plague occurs and it is not a fracture, then consider: if it is from a blow with a spearhead or similar object, and the bone has already broken only on its own and it is a large wound, and you fear that an abscess will develop in that patient, then immediately perform phlebotomy of the cephalic vein, and do not delay; and remove as much blood as possible according to the strength of the blow, unless there is some reason prohibiting phlebotomy, especially if the blood that has flowed from the wound is little.
And let the phlebotomy be on the opposite side of the wounded part; and keep the patient from exertion and wine and coarse foods.
But if for some reason you forbid phlebotomy, then let him be put on a low diet and not approach flesh nor wine.
And pause over the wound if an abscess develops, then apply hot oil or wine that has been thickened with flour.
But if you are sure that an abscess will develop, then pause over the wound while it is still fresh with its own blood and the air has not yet changed that powder which I will recommend later on a small scale.
And if the air has already changed it, then pause over the abscess and let it drain until it is healed.
But if the wound is large or it has occurred from an incision with a spearhead or similar object and its edges are not fitting together by themselves, then adjust those edges with stitches according to what I will recommend for the stitching of lips.
But if the wound is already exposed to bone and tendon, and there is only a slight suspension of the flesh, then incise it and cure the wound with medicines and restore the flesh properly in place of bone, and command the patient to be put on a diet of coarse foods such as cabbage and beans and similar ones until he is healed.
And if you find putrefaction in the bone and it does not adhere to the bone, then incise all that is rotten and remove it, and then cure it.
But if in these wounds an artery or vein from which blood is flowing can occur and it cannot be ligated by medicines, then inquire about the artery; and if you find that one has not been incised, then incise it with a scalpel, or tie it. And if necessity compels you to do what I have said does not suit, then cauterize until the blood is stopped.
And if these wounds are simple and small, then their cause is light. Therefore you powder them with this powder so that it may solidify before the air changes them.
And the manner of the powder is this: take one part oil of sesame seeds, two parts dragon's blood, three parts myrrh ground; let it all be finely ground and sifted, and with that fill the wound, and let it be pressed down by good pressure until it adheres to it, and then let it coagulate with its own blood.
And then press it down from above with powders and leave it like that; do not remove it while it is like this until it becomes an abscess, for the medicine will not be removed from it until it is healed.
And sometimes you can do this alone with just cauterization when you do not have sesame oil and dragon's blood present.
And this same operation is done in large wounds when it is appropriate to pause over them and press them down, especially fresh ones with their own blood which the air has not yet altered.
And if the air has altered them, and especially in summer time, then it is not fitting to use this powder. But at such times cure them with what I have said, so that you put over them some fresh ointments or polish them with flour paste mixed with water and honey until they are cleansed of pus; and then cure them with the other remedies until they are healed.
If you encounter a small fracture in bone during an operation, then extract it using tweezers.
Then I will teach you the treatment of head fractures that are dangerous.
Of the wounds of the neck
But if the wound occurs in the neck, then there is no difference in treatment between this wound and a simple head wound.
But if the nerve or artery of the neck is injured, then if it is a nerve, there is no hope for recovery except to avoid treatment with anything that causes strong contraction, such as vitriol and similar substances that irritate nerves. And do not apply any caustic substance to the wound for fear of burning the nerve, because the substance of nerves is fragile and their continuity extends to the brain, which is the pulse center of all members.
And if you treat it with mild medicines, such as washing it with rosewater or applying it diluted in olive oil (with or without roses), and bandages when washed with rosewater, and other soft minerals according to this method, and then wrap it gently.
But if the wound is large, then apply sutures to close the lips of the wound and afterward dress it with powders until it heals.
But if the wound is deep or if it has happened that part of the nerve has been cut off, then pierce it in the most depressed place with a needle.
"However, if in the wound an artery has already been cut and there is blood flow, then separate or seal that, or ligate that, or cauterize that if necessary."
"If the spines of the coccyx have already been cut or all, and the veins of the rectum are saved, then adjust the lips of the buttocks with suture over the canal of the coccyx without touching that; Afterwards equalize that and reduce it to its natural shape, and support it with suitable strapping, and leave it for several days; And afterwards care for it with ointments in which there is astringency and excitation until it is healed."
"If the wound has already reached the bone, then explore that and if there are fragments of bone, remove all those that you can; And whatever is not apparent to you, leave it until the wound closes, and let it separate naturally, and its inflammation be alleviated."
"And if the wound is fresh then sprinkle over it the powder which I have recommended to you." If a fistula is made in the anus, then treat it with that remedy of which mention will be made shortly in its chapter.
If it is a wound from a lance or knife, and sometimes its depth varies, then consider more if there is wind coming out of the wound when the patient breathes; then know that the wound is fatal.
And if it is not deep and the wound is fresh with its own blood, then you pause in it for the first hour with powdered plantain, and do not press it so that no blood is retained in the depth of it and returns to the heart and increases the illness, but rather pause it with an attractive ointment, and cleanse it twice daily.
And if the ointment is not at hand, then pause in the wound with cotton moistened so that it draws out whatever moisture there may be; and make sure that the patient sleeps on the wound so that what is inside it may flow out.
But if three days have passed since the wound and there has been no spasm or trembling of the heart nor constriction of the lungs in the patient, and other good conditions of it are seen, then know that the wound is healed; and then cure it with poultices and other treatments until it is completely healed.
But if the healing of it is prevented, and it has been open all this time, then know that it has already become a fistula; cure it according to its chapter.
And if the wound is from a cut by a sword or knife and it is simple on the surface of the foot or hand, then cure it with what is preceded by suturing if it is large, or with powder if it is small.
But if there has already been injury to the bone and pieces of it have already been cut off, then you turn the wound and try to extract those pieces, if they are separate. But if they are not separate, then leave them inside until the wound heals, for their extraction will be easier that way.
And concerning other accidental wounds on other limbs, the judgment regarding their treatment is as we have said.
Of abdominal wounds.
"Indisposition that occurs in the belly may be large, or small, or moderate."
"And small rupture is done with difficulty in another way, and so its reduction is more difficult if you do not quickly extract them from their place at once, because they open and become swollen so that the entrance of them becomes difficult."
"And therefore the best rupture is moderate, because in that one it is not difficult to reduce the intestine, just as it is difficult in the two kinds mentioned above."
"And know that there are four ways to suture the belly, but two of them are common and convenient for sutures of other wounds of the body."
"And the other two sutures are proper to other wounds, but however they are more proper to the suture of the belly."
"And I tell you each one with explanation and description."
"Therefore it is said that when the wound is small and some cause of the intestine comes out through it, and it is difficult to reduce it, then this is in one of two ways: either because of the smallness of the rupture as we have said, or when the intestine has come into inflammation because of the coldness of the air."
"And therefore when this is the case, then you should cut it so that you immerse a sponge or wet cloth in hot water alone, or take some hot water with squinant, cyperus, spice, and embrocatum with which you moisturize the intestine inside until the inflammation has been resolved."
"And sometimes it happens that there is putrefaction in the wound, and it is better to use water alone for the resolution of inflammation."
"And therefore when you see that the inflammation has been resolved, then you should moisten the intestine with water in which is cooked mallow and malva, for by this means it is alleviated from inflammation with little cause."
"But if the inflammation of the intestine has not been alleviated by this treatment, then cut the rupture a little with an instrument with which you have incisedemorroids."
"And the first treatment is better, for it is proper that it not be a section, and there should be no occupation to cut unless necessary and unavoidable."
"Concerning the instrument, see its form:"
"The one part of it is cut sharp and the other not-sharp, and the extremity is subtle but not too delicate, rather somewhat blunt."
"And therefore when the wound has been enlarged and the intestine comes out through it, then its reduction should be according to its natural form in its proper place if possible about that, for better is."
"But when the rupture is wide and is in the lower part of the belly, then you should make the patient lie on his back and place their buttocks higher than their head; and if it is in the upper part of the belly, then you should place the head down and the feet higher than the buttocks."
"And likewise if the rupture is in one of the two parts of the belly, then always place your intention and consideration on this so that the part where the wound is may be higher than the other."
"And therefore you should administer this in large wounds and in moderate wounds."
"And in small wounds, pause until it is prepared and make sure that the one who ministers it is among your most experienced, who holds the rupture entirely with his hand and adjusts the lips of it, and quickly discovers from that to that which sews any cause if necessary."
"And this is the common manner of suturing: first take a needle or count needles according to the quantity of the width of the wound; and then leave it at the end of the rupture on the tip of your finger, and thread the needle with one thread, but do not put any knot in both ends of the thread, with two knots that are left below the thread, inside which you make it penetrate from one part to another; and you have already attached four threads."
"And then thread with a double knot around the needle, and sometimes two parts together, and then attach both lips and the wound by proper attachment; and then leave the thickness of your finger and put another needle in that, and then tie it with thread like the first needle; and do not cease doing this until you have completed all the contraction of the wound."
"And let the needles be moderate between thickness and subtlety, for thin needles cut flesh too lightly; and thick ones are difficult to thread with the thread, therefore they should be moderate in both thickness and subtlety."
"And it is not necessary for the needle to be stuck in both ends of the thread at once, lest the flesh be cut too lightly and the wound be opened before its consolidation."
"And do not prolong suturing so that the wound is not hindered from healing."
"And then cut the ends of the needles so that the patient does not bother with their sleep; and you will place powdered breadcrumbs on all parts over the suture, which hold the ends of the needles; and leave them until you know that the wound is healed."
"And these types of suturing with needles in any manner are more convenient for small wounds, because one needle or two is enough for their suturing."
"But the second type of suturing is like this: you should use four threads for suturing, from the thread and two knots at once, with a needle that has fine silk wrapped around it in both thickness and subtlety."
"And then, when the needle has pierced these four extremities, return the needle to that same opening from which you began, so that the wound draws back its pus-filled cavity into the abscess, so that the suture may be made according to a stitch of cloth with which the wounds are strengthened."
"And pause between each suture the quantity of the thickness of the little finger."
"And this suture is known by men."
"And at this suture you cauterized the wound which was inflicted on a man in his belly who had been struck with a dagger, and the disruption of the wound was more than a palm, and it was issued from the bowels around two palms of the bowels near the middle place, and the disruption was in the middle of the member; and then you reduced that deposit which the bowels had flowed out of the wound for 24 hours."
"And the wound was consolidated in the space of about 15 days, and that man was cured and healed; and at that time he lived for many years, and remained in his usual condition."
"And the other physicians had judged that he would not be healed; and it was by miracle that he was cured, because you did not cure him with an ointment, since he was in a place where no ointment could be applied nor any medicine, but you paused over the wound twice a day and washed it assiduously with water of honey until it was healed."
"But you describe two kinds of suture proper according to the narrative of the Word."
"And it is that you begin with the stitching of the cord, and insert the needle from without to within."
"And then as the needle penetrates into the cord and meets with it in length along all the body, let the extremity of the thread remain in that which you have inserted the needle; and make the needle penetrate into the other extremity from within outwards in the other extremity of the member."
"And then when you have made it penetrate thus, afterwards make it penetrate again in that same extremity of the member from without within; and let the extremity of the thread remain on this side, and make the needle penetrate into the other extremity from within outwards."
"And make it penetrate again with that penetration with which you have made it penetrate in the thread at the extremity of the member which is on the inside, so that all may penetrate."
"And then begin from this same side and draw it with the extremity which is of the thread on the other side, and withdraw the needle from the cord which has penetrated, and reduce that in that cord and tie the extremity of the thread which is on the other side with this extremity of the member; and withdraw that from the cord which is on the part within."
"And do this once and again, and do it once more afterwards until you have tied all that is without according to that example."
"And the sum of this manner of suture is that you make a stitch of skin with which you sew the skin, so that you make the thread once from the extremity of the cord and let it remain again until you have completed it."
"But the second kind of proper suture which you describe expressly, and this is about it and for it to be sewn together, is that you sew it in half-length so that some physicians sew it thus, arranging every part with its corresponding part according to nature; and they apply the extremity of one to the other extremity and the extremity of the member to the other extremity of it, and this is done as you command."
"So that you leave the needle in the extremity of the member near the outside part, and make it penetrate within that part and let both extremities of the thread remain; and then turn the needle round and make it penetrate from without within at both extremities of the thread."
"And then turn those loops round, and make each loop penetrate from within outwards in two extremities of the member other than those which are on the opposite side."
"And this manner of suture is better than common light suture, and it is the suture of which there was a preceding mention."
"This is the discourse of Galen"
"And others say that the suture of the belly is corrected with two needles, so that you insert in each a thread and begin with an introduction of the needle on whichever side it is necessary for you to sew according to the suture of those who sew the heart ingeniously."
"And know that when a disruption occurs in the middle part of the belly, then the suture of it is more difficult than those of other parts of the belly."
"But the judgment of medical treatment of pleurisy is also the judgment of other plagues."
"The cause is because when you succeed in the recent plague with its pure blood before the air alters it and reduces the vessel and sews it up well and applies it properly afterwards, then it remains calm on that inflammatory dust."

"But if you are not present with the medications then it remains calm for a short time because as soon as it begins to throw forth much sweat and bad humours and changes twice a day, as you have taught us, until it is healed, because in many dispositions when the plagues are simple you do not need other medication."
"But if you fear that the plague may communicate to an injury of the principal members then it is necessary for you to immerse lion's wool in pure olive oil or rose oil and apply it around those parts which are between the angles and leave them thus."
"And if there is pain or putrefaction in its vessels because many times this happens then crystallize it with black treacle and vinegar, especially if the putrefaction has reached the vessel and a penetrating evacuation has been made into its concavity."
"And know that that which is in the thick vessel is of lighter healing than that which is in the subtle vessels."
"And it is of difficult healing because the vessel which is called 'gungu' does not receive healing from any plague that falls into it completely; and this is because of the great multitude of veins that are in it and the magnitude of them that are in those, and because of the subtlety of its body, and because of its proximity to the nature of nerves."
"But if what proceeds from the plague is tissue and you succeed in it recently then reduce it according to your discretion with which you reduce vessels ingeniously."
"But if it has passed into the space and is now green or black then stretch it with a thread over that part which is darkened by it, so that there comes a flow of blood because in the tissue are veins and arteries."
"And then incise that which is other than the thread and leave two extremities of the thread hanging from the part beyond the plague outside it, so that over you may be relieved the attraction of it you must have the stitching of the tissue and emission of the sweat of the plague."
"Remembrance of the plagues when they occur in the vessel."
"When there is a disruption in the vessel and it is small then it is possible that it may be restored in some people because I have seen this man who was struck with a spear wound in his belly which was a plague on the right side of the stomach and the plague was old and had made a fistula, but from it came management and windiness."
Then I pursue the healing of him though it was not yet completed in his recovery, but ceased to explore that region which had been healed and the place is consolidated.
And I saw that the place was already consolidated, so I told him to be careful not to aggravate his condition by eating and drinking too much, or overexerting himself, and to avoid excessive bathing and exercise.
And some experienced people say that when the bowel moves and is narrow, it should be tied in this manner: take figs with large heads, adjust both lips of the movement, and place one of those figs with its mouth open over both lips of the movement. Then press on it until its head separates from it, because it adheres and does not dissolve.
And place another fig near the first one, and continue doing so with figs one after the other according to the amount of movement there is.
Then reduce that and tie it with the movement; and those attached heads will remain inside the bowel until the bowel is healed, without causing any harm to the patient.
And it is possible that the bowel may be tied with a fine thread made from the bowel of an animal attached to it, because it is more like a needle. You should take the end of these bowel threads, and make sure it is well cleaned, and tie the end of it with the thread you have, wrapping it around, and then insert that thread through the needle and sew it onto the bowel, reducing it at the point of disruption.
And this manner of suturing with figs is nothing but a matter of trust and hope.
But if the movement is large and wide, especially if it is in one of the subtle bowels, because then it will only result in subtlety and not in the healing of it entirely.
Of the cure for hemorrhoids and fistulas.
"I know that every ulcer and abscess, when it opens and becomes ancient, turns into an ulcer that does not heal and continually discharges pus without being cut open; universally this is called a fistula, which we call that wound."
"A fistula is indeed a hard, tough, white nodosity with which there is no pain and it has a cavity just like the cavity of a bird's egg; because of this it is called that hollow wound."
"And in some men there is moistness [that causes] an ulcer which discharges pus; but if the moisture is cut away, it heals in a few hours." "Sometimes this moisture is much, little, thick, and subtle."
"I have already explained all those causes, their symptoms and the treatment of them by medicine in the division [of ulcers]."
"And it is necessary that I should also tell you about the cure of fistula, which is done by operation with a knife."
"And know that fistulas occur in all the members of the body: some of them extend to large veins and arteries, or to nerves, or to the bladder, or to some part of the spine, or to some of the joints composed by composition such as those of the hand and foot; and others open near the main member and its like."
"And therefore those fistulas which are of this kind are among the illnesses which are difficult to heal and do not receive cure, and dealing with them is troublesome and ignorant."
"And if among the fistulas there is one whose depth does not reach these places which I have mentioned, and you hope for its cure and trust in it, then take a thread of wool or iron and try to find that with it."
"But if the fistula is winding, then investigate it with a thread of thin lead, for lead with the lightness of its body is eased and curved along the winding."
"And if the fistula has many horrible openings, it will not be possible for you to mark them with a thread."
"Then cauterize the openings separately, because the moisture by which you cauterize it will go towards the other openings and from them."
"And then inquire carefully to see if you can know whether here there are bones or nerves; and also whether the fistula is far or near; or whether it is one with many openings which is located on top of everything with your utmost strength, investigation, compression with the hand over the place, and similar signs and causes accidentally occurring in ulcers."
"And when you have considered all those causes with careful observation, then come to the treatment according to your judgment: and this is that you consider whether it is an apparent fistula near in a healthy place, far from a joint, nerve, artery, vein, or one of the places which I have mentioned."
"Then dry out the fistula according to what has been said above about its narration, and remove that which is in that filtration and of corrupted flesh, and that which is born from the opening of the flesh or of the skin and similar things, and cure it so that it may be healed."
"But if the fistula is of great depth and is winding, then it is necessary that you insert it into the front as much as possible according to your ability, and also cleanse it from all its corrupted flesh; and then administer bandages wrapped in sharp medicines, and introduce those into the cavity of the fistula which you have grasped with an iron hook."
"And do this for several days in succession so that the sharp medicine may burn away all that is rough and corrupted within the cavity of the fistula."
"Then restore it with dressings which generate healthy flesh until it is healed."
If it does not heal by this method, then cauterize according to what we have advised.
If the cause of the fistula is bone and it needs to be certified, then inquire about it and dry it according to what we have advised, if you do not prohibit any cause of vein or nerve or main member as we have said.
But if the bone is exposed and there is some corruption and blackness in it, then remove that within which all the corruption has gathered; and afterwards cure it with this until it heals.
And if it does not heal and throws out again as it did before, then know that you have not reached the complete eradication of the corruption; therefore, uncover it once more and carefully examine its cause and clean it with your strongest ointment, and afterwards restore it.
And then if it is healed, well and good. But if not, then know that that corruption is in the deep interior of the body, which has not been reached, and therefore in that case there is nothing to do but leave it alone.
And if the corrupted bone is small, or can be removed, then remove it with fine forceps suitable for that purpose.
But if there are many bones, then carefully perform the extraction of all of them, and do not leave behind any cause with your strength.
But if you encounter any difficulty due to moisture, and there is no fear or error in their incision, then cut those membranes or flesh if it is here, and deliver the bones.
But if you are not prepared to remove the bones at that moment, then pause over the wound until it is closed up again, and leave that within which that closing has taken place around those flesh bones and membranes, and guard the wound so that it does not harden, and keep the incision you have made in your operation open.
Have then, if you fear, a poultice soaked in treacle and honey, or in Egyptian pitch, or in some other green ointment, for when those membranes dry up and the bones are separated by ablation, attraction is relieved.
But if it is a large bone such as the thighbone or shinbone or similar ones, and only the surface of it is corrupted, then cut away that corruption only behind, until that blackness and corruption is removed, and then restore the wound.
But if that which is corrupted in it is a large part, and the corruption has reached the marrow of the bone, then it is necessary to close up that and cut off all around where the corruption has penetrated, and then cure it until it is consolidated.
And I recommend that you have with you something belonging to a man in his shinbone, so that you may pause on it as an example and assistant for your operation.
There was once a young man about thirty years old, to whom pain occurred in his shinbone, and the cause of that pain was inside the thigh bone within which matter had penetrated into the shinbone, and it was a matter of an abscess with a large swelling, and there was no external cause for it.
And then much time passed with that one because of the error of physicians while the abscess was growing, and much matter came out from it, and his treatment was finally stopped when the thighbone became fistulated, and he did many things through those orificial parts which were all emitting pus and moisture from the body.
And then for a long time he was treated by many doctors around two years, and there was not much knowledge among them but rather skill, until I was called.
And when I saw the thighbone of that one and the matter that was running out from those orificial parts through a large part of his body, then that man's whole body was already emaciated and his complexion was yellowish.
And then I inserted the tent into one of those orificial parts and reached the bone with it.
"And then examine and probe all the orifices and find those through which fluid comes from every part of the chamber."
"And then you cut and incise on one of those orifices where you discovered a fracture of the bone, and you removed that decayed part which was earthy and rotten and blackened; and already a part of the chamber into which it had entered was corrupted."
"And then you closed what I had discovered and prepared of the bone discovered."
"I feared that it was not merely a fracture but some corruption which had been hidden and closed up, for I had already dressed the wound."
"And therefore he paused the restoration of the plague by using medicine in a consolidative way for too long, but it was not consolidated."
"Furthermore, I explored and exposed the bone a second time over the previous discovery, revealing continuous corruption in the bone."
"And I closed what appeared to be that corruption, and therefore he was perforated fairly for the cure of it and restoration, but it was not restored."
"And then I discovered it again and did not cease to incise the bone little by little particularly, perforating the restoration of it, but it was not restored until he had incised around a palm's width, and that extracted with its marrow, and therefore he restored it with medicines, and it is lightly consolidated and healed."
"It is not necessary to iterate the operation and section of it unless for the position of the friability of it and for the scarcity of its tolerance and fear of its death, because it had syncope in all hours due to superfuility of evacuation."
"And therefore it is healed by whole healing, and nothing is in place of hard flesh; and its position is good in its body and returns the virtue of it; and it has been converted into its positions and does not do anything contrary to it in walking nor harm in any cause."
"But if it is prominent in place of the body already broken, then you should cut it this way: Take linen and strengthen that in the extremity of that prominent bone, and order someone to stretch that out; And pause that linen of wool thicker than the first linen; And therefore tie that over the flesh that is left near the bone, and extend the extremity of it so that you draw the flesh apart from there, and you uncover the flesh upon the place where you want to saw so that the saw does not cut the flesh."
"And pause a piece of wood or board near the bone decently, because when you do this the saw will not cut the corrupted flesh."
"And it is necessary that the sawing be little by little upon the corrupted place because if it is in the concavity of the corrupt bone and does not appear in its appearance to the feeling, then the sawing must be done again."
"And if the bone is corrupted but not prominent, then one part continues with the other, and the corruption is in the middle place or at the end of it. Then uncover the flesh from all parts; And therefore pause wood near by, and saw that first part where there is corruption until the sawing of the other part is continuous."
"And let the sawing be according to the place of the corruption little by little, as we have said."
"And if the corruption is at the joint, then cut that corrupted joint, and saw the bone where it continues from the other part."
"But if the corruption is in the continuation of two joints, then it is not in its reason but by chance."
"And if the corruption is in the breast of the hand or foot, it is very difficult; however you should investigate the corruption in whatever way it appears to you, and remove that, and cleanse that according to every disposition which is possible for you, and with each invention be rectified by you when it does not cause any contradiction to vein or nerve."
"And know that there are different types of saws and sawing tools for cutting these bones. They are made according to the situation of the bones, their preparation, thickness, subtlety, size, smallness, hardness, and rarity; therefore you should prepare suitable instruments for each type of operation."
"And know that this operation implies to you regarding the type of instrument which you need when with you is great study and long knowledge of the methods of this art, and experience in the ways of diseases because then you already knew what is suitable for each tool according to each disease."

Therefore, in that case, you should incise that member where the corruption has occurred so that the illness is cured through death or mischief which is a greater impairment of the member.
The sign of that which happens is that the member becomes black where it was burned by fire or approaches darkness where the corruption has entered within that member and takes all the body. Therefore, you should incise there.
Similarly, if it is caused by corruption due to some venomous causes such as the sting of a marine scorpion or viper or rattlesnake and similar ones.
And if the corruption or the injury is at the tip of the finger, then you should incise the finger and not allow the corruption to spread into the hand.
Similarly, if it spreads to the hand, then you should incise there from the wrist of the firearm and not allow the corruption to spread into the forearm.
And if it reaches up there, then you should incise the arm at the elbow in the joint.
And if the corruption passes beyond that and sometimes surrounds the elbow, then in that case it is the death of the illness. And to administer another cause for cure other than that is a matter of quantity of virtue.
Similarly, when corruption reaches the finger of the foot, then you should incise there to one of the joints
And if it takes hold in the ankle of the foot, then you should amputate all of the foot. But if it can enter into the knee, then you should incise the calf at the joint of the knee
And if corruption has already reached over the knee, then in that case there is no help but release and let the illness take its course to death.
The manner of incising the member or sawing it is that you should stretch one bandage at the point where you wish to incise, and stretch another bandage above that place. And extend one bandage towards the points below, and extend another bandage above them. And separate the flesh which is between two bandages with a wide knife so that all the flesh is exposed. And then it should be incised or sawn.
And care should be taken to place cloth of lime on all sides so that it does not touch the place raw, and that wound may come to the illness with proper lesion and caustic aposteme.
But if bleeding occurs while working, then you should cauterize the place carefully, or place some powder on it to stop the bleeding. And then return to your medication until it is complete.
And then bind the member with a bandage in whatever way seems appropriate, and treat it until it is healed.
And I relate to you what happened to a man in his foot, which is the accident that I and you are discussing, which was that it became black in his foot with burn-like discoloration resembling fire combustion.
And this corruption first occurred in his toe such that it spread throughout the entire foot
And then that man prepared to cut off his foot himself because the cure was not going well due to its severity of pain and burning. And he incised his foot at the joint, and fire healed it.
For a long time that same corruption occurred in the index finger of his hand
And then I came to him, and he told me that that same corruption had spread over with what I had placed on his hand as medicine, especially the cleansing of his body. And the corruption did not spread back but began to go into another finger until it reached the hand
And he asked me to incise his hand, and I did not want to do that hoping for the repercussion of that corruption. And more so because I feared the death of the incision of his hand, since the strength of the illness was already established
And since he left me, I heard that that man had returned to his land and had incised all of his hand himself, and it healed.
And I have not related this narrative except to help with what is known about this illness, and that it may be understood for which it is named and according to which it should be treated.
Concerning the treatment of sinus and the quality of cleansing with medicines
When an aposteme occurs on some fleshy members and the space of the aposteme becomes prolonged so that it collects pus, and then it breaks and perforates, and the pus is discharged from it, and the place remains void as if it were a vessel, and the channel that is above it is like a thin cloth, and no further corruption reaches it, and it does not print on bone or nerve or tendon, it is called a sinus, and it is not named fistula.
But if the space is prolonged so that corruption impresses on some member, then it is called fistula and notzukem.
"And the treatment of this condition is to insert that chain completely in this manner as it is rolled up, especially when it has been subtiliated and made with cloth, ensuring that it does not adhere to the location due to its corruption."
"If however you suspect that the chain has adhered and that this corruption cannot be achieved by any other means, then at that time you should treat him with a clyster."
"And if you consider the sinus, and if it is large, and the arm that goes in has a foul odor, then clysterize him with an Egyptian medicine which is made of oil and sour wine and cinnamon ground together equally, put in a vessel, and cooked over the fire until it reaches the consistency of honey."
"And moreover take of that which is necessary and dissolve it with water and honey; and clysterize him with this mixture into the sinus, and strengthen the orifice of it, and leave the medicine in there for the quantity of two hours."
"And then remove that with a sponge; and do this for so many days until the sinus is cleaned and the pus removed."
"And sometimes it is clysterized with hot ash water when this medicine is not present. And if you take the ashes of figs and put them on the water, then collect that and clysterize him with it until you are satisfied that the sinus has been cleaned."
"And if the patient cannot tolerate the Egyptian medicine or hot ash water, then clysterize him with warm water and honey mixed together three times, and clysterize him with wine and honey mixed, for it is proper that honey should cleanse and wash, and wine makes the sinus adhere, especially when there is an abundance of astringency and dryness in the wine."
"And when you have done this several times and are satisfied that the sinus has been removed, then clysterize him with something that makes flesh grow in it."
"And take of refined diaphoretic and dissolve it with rose oil and astringent wine, or clysterize him with some other medicines and ointments that have the properties which have already been written about in the treatise on ointments."
"And if the orifice of the sinus is narrow so that the cannula of the clyster cannot be received there, then gradually dilate it with a little iron, and pause in it with hot water wrapped in Egyptian ointment or basilicon ointment until it has been dilated."
"And similarly, if the orifice is wide, then gather its lips with a suture and leave in it the quantity in which the clyster enters without addition."
"And if the opening of it from which the arm comes out is elevated above its parts, then dry that place with a poultice below where it is located so that the arm may run easily, for when the arm is obstructed in the concavity of the sinus flesh may be generated there."

"And also consider the place where that sinus is located, if the patient feels pain there or not, and whether it is an abscess."

For there are some people in whom the generation of flesh in the wounds is delayed, and among those are also those in whom it happens otherwise."
"If the sinus has remained dry for many days without discharging any matter, then you should know that the sinus is not adhering. If the medications are humid in their substance and virtue, they will be dry like fine ointment when they have reached the appropriate amount of addition of pitch."
